		'//www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js';

<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

The antenna is designed to operate at 915 MHz. Its electrical size is (λ<sub>0</sub>/30)×(λ<sub>0</sub>/30), which makes it among the smallest antennas presented in literature. The new antenna has a “Vivaldi-like” aperture fed with a slot line coupled electromagnetically to a microstrip line. The aperture is loaded with a meander line. The new antenna is thoroughly investigated both theoretically and experimentally. It enjoys a number of appealing characteristics, such as compact size, low profile, flexible impedance tuning, good impedance bandwidth, omnidirectional radiation patterns, low cross-polarization level, and reasonable gain.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>The radio frequency identification (RFID) transponder (tag) consists of a microchip packaged together with an antenna. The tag’s antenna has to be small in size and light in weight, as it is attached to the object that would be identified. It should be also inexpensive for mass production. Moreover, it should have omnidirectional radiation pattern so that the reader and transponder can communicate with each other independent on their relative direction. In addition, the tag’s antenna should also be easily integrated with active devices. The design of the RFID tag antenna is a tradeoff between size reduction and performance. Based on that, the research in this area can be classified into four categories. These categories are listed, and representative samples of each are cited in the following paragraph.</p><p>The first category aims at decreasing the antenna size dramatically even if this comes against its performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. The second category targets the enhancement of the antenna performance regardless of its size <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. By the antenna performance, we mean its radiation efficiency and gain, which affect the maximum communication range between the reader and tag antennas. The third category is midway between category 1 and category 2, where compromise between small size and good performance has been performed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. The fourth category is concerned with designing a dual-band antenna serving different RFID frequency bands <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, or RFID/WLAN bands <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>.</p><p>This letter presents a novel antenna that belongs to the first category, where size reduction is the major concern. It is tuned for operation at 915 MHz. Its size is 10.67×10.67 mm<sup>2</sup>, which corresponds to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\lambda _{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the free-space wavelength. The structure of the proposed antenna together with a parametric study are presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>. The theoretical and experimental characterizations of the new antenna are presented and discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>. The important conclusions are stated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Geometry of the proposed RFID tag antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Structure and Parametric Study</h2></div><p>The proposed RFID tag antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. It features a “Vivaldi-like” aperture terminated by a meander line. The function of this line is to increase the electrical dimensions of the antenna without increasing the overall size significantly. This has been achieved by winding the line in a compact area, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The aperture is excited via a coplanar slot line that is located together with the aperture at one side of a dielectric substrate. This slot line is electromagnetically coupled to a perpendicular microstrip feeding line that runs at the other side of the substrate, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The electrical lengths of both the slot and microstrip lines are very small. Hence, these lines must be considered as part of the antenna rather than feeding transmission lines. The coaxial cable or chip feeding the antenna should be connected to the terminals of the very short microstrip line. The proposed antenna is designed to be fabricated on FR4 substrate with thickness of 0.8 mm and dielectric constant of 4.4. The metal on both sides of the substrate is copper with thickness of 17 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-25" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m.</p><p>The overall size of the proposed RFID tag antenna tuned at 915 MHz is as small as 10.67×10.67 mm<sup>2</sup>. This physical size corresponds to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-28" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-size: 70.7%; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.3em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">(\lambda _{0} /30) ^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. These parameters are thoroughly optimized using HFSS <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a> to achieve best matching with two values of impedance. The first value is the regular 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-125" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; Similarly, the reactive part of the impedance turns from capacitive into inductive as both parameters are increasing, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>.

<p></p><p>Two points are marked in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a) and (b)</a>. At Point 1, the antenna is matched with a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-299" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> system, with the real part very close to 50 and imaginary part very close to zero. The antenna at this point is matched to the network analyzer system. The coordinates of this point are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-302" role="math" style="width: 6.73em; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.84em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-340" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">X<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-341"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-343" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-345" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-346" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">100</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-347" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">X _{\rm in} = 100 \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are almost intersecting with each other, i.e., the antenna is conjugately matched to the chip impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-348" role="math" style="width: 6.309em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.649em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.59em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-349"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-350" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-351" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">77</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-352" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-353" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-354" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">100</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-355" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-356" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">(77 -j 100) \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The coordinates of this point, i.e., the optimum values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-357" role="math" style="width: 2.706em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.4em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-358"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-359"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-360" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-361"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-362"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-363" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-364" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-365" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-366" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">L _{\rm mean}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-367" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.87em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-368"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-369"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-370" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-371"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-372"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-373" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-374" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-375" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-376" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">L _{\rm line}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for conjugate matching with the chip, are 4.790 and 9.376 mm, respectively. It is worth mentioning that although one representative chip is adopted, the impedance tuning of the proposed antenna is very flexible and can be performed for any other chip impedance.</p><p>In order to be able to measure the proposed antenna using a conventional network analyzer system, only the version with 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-377" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-378"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-379" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> input impedance is fabricated. Conventional printed circuit board (PCB) technology is used for fabrication. Photographs of the fabricated prototype are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, in which the feeding 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-380" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-381"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-382" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> SMA connector can be seen.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Photographs of the fabricated prototype (the adjacent ruler is in centimeters): (a) front side and (b) back side.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results and Discussions</h2></div><p>All results presented in this section belong to the 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-383" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-384"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-385" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> version of the proposed antenna. The current distribution in vector format on the radiating side of the antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, as calculated using HFSS at 915 MHz. It is clear that the current is intensive on the meander line of the antenna. However, the current on the horizontal long arms is flowing in opposite directions, which results in negligible radiation. On the other hand, the short vertical arms’ current is flowing in unified direction, as marked in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. This current is the main source of radiation from the proposed antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Current distribution at 915 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The return loss of the proposed antenna has been measured by placing it inside an anechoic metallic box, whose inner walls are covered with absorbers. The antenna under test is connected to the vector network analyzer via a coaxial cable mounted to the SMA connector of the antenna. One port calibration has been performed using short, open, and load calibration standards. The return loss of the proposed antenna is plotted versus frequency in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> as simulated using both HFSS and CST <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3">[16]</a>, together with measurements. It is clear that the three curves agree very well with each other. The measured resonance frequency is 914.5 MHz, which is very close to the design value of 915 MHz. The measured −10-dB impedance bandwidth of this antenna is 3%, which is reasonable for such miniaturized antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Measured and simulated return loss versus frequency.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The 3-D radiation pattern of the proposed antenna is “donut” in shape as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, based on the CST calculations at 915 MHz. The antenna radiates bidirectional from both sides of the substrate. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-386" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-388" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-389" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-390"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-391" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-392" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">xz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane) cut is circular, which means isotropic radiation along this plane. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-393" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-394"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-395" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane perpendicular cut, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-396" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-397"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-398" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-399" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">yz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane, has a figure-eight shape with maximum at broadside and minimum at endfire direction. The orientations of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-400" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-402" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>- and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-403" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-404"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-405" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-planes are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The radiation pattern measurements of the proposed antenna have been performed inside a conventional anechoic chamber specified for measurements within the RF and microwave range of frequencies, i.e., from 1 until 30 GHz. No special preparations have been made in order to isolate the SMA connector. The antenna under test is mounted on a small wooden fixture at the receiving side, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>3-D gain pattern at 915 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Wooden fixture used to hold antennas under test (AUTs) inside the anechoic chamber.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> shows the measured and CST-calculated radiation patterns in both the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-406" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-407"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-408" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-409" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-410"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-411" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-412" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">xz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-413" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-414"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-415" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-416" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-417"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-418" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-419" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">yz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). Normalized gain patterns are displayed in this figure. In the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-420" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-421"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-422" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane, the upper half of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, the calculated copolar component is uniform as expected. The measured copolar component shows similar behavior except around the endfire direction from one side. This can be attributed to the parasitic effects of the SMA connector whose size is about the same as the antenna itself, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. The measured cross-polarization level at broadside is about −30 dB and significantly increases at endfire directions. According to CST simulation, the cross-polarization level in this plane is less than −28 dB.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6289338/6289338-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Measured and calculated radiation patterns at 915 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6289338/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As for the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-423" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-424"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-425" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane, the lower half of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, the simulated copolar component has the well-known figure-eight shape. The measured copolar component agrees well with simulation around the broadside direction, while deviation occurs at endfire due to the presence of the SMA connector. Although the feeding connector affects the measured radiation patterns, these patterns are still acceptable. This suggests that the feeding chip, which will be located at the same position of the SMA connector, will impose acceptable degradation on the radiation patterns. The measured cross-polarization level is around −17 dB at broadside, with a maximum level of −12 dB. The calculated cross-polarization level in this plane is less than −26 dB.</p><p>Although only half of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-426" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-427"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-428" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>- and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-429" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-430"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-431" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-planes are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, the other halves are identical, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, and are omitted. It is worth mentioning that simulations reveal that the second version of this antenna conjugately matched to the microchip shows similar radiation characteristics to those presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 6</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">8</a>.</p><p>The calculated directivity, gain, and radiation efficiency at 915 MHz are 2.13 dBi, −2.97 dBi, and 31%, respectively. The maximum measured realized gain at 915 MHz in the broadside direction is −3.75 dBi, which is close to the calculated one. These values of gain and efficiency are quite reasonable for such an electrically very small antenna.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A novel RFID tag antenna is presented in this letter. Its electrical dimensions are as small as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-432" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.787em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1003.79em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-433"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-434" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-435"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-436" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-437"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-438"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-439" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-440"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-441"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-442" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-443" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">30</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-444"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.3em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-445" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-446"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-447"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-448" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">(\lambda _{0} /30) ^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The proposed antenna is very convenient for RFID tags that put severe restriction on size. Although it has been prepared for operation at 915 MHz, it can be easily tuned to any other frequency of operation. The new antenna is fabricated and measured. It has been also analyzed theoretically using two well-known commercial software packages. The very good agreement between simulations and measurements validates the appealing features of the new antenna.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
